**One new insight captured:**
- **Insight-219** (`docs/insights/219-validated-input-must-reach-destination.md`) — when an API route, harness handler, or workflow input accepts a user-driven value, the route must trace that value to the side-effecting call where it has effect. Validation is necessary but insufficient — code that validates an input and never uses it is a silent UX failure that compiles cleanly. Brief 221's `/api/v1/review/[token]/approve` accepted `selectedKind`, validated it against the server-stamped eligibility list, then called `dispatchWorkItem({...})` WITHOUT setting `workItems.runnerOverride = selectedKind` — so the dispatcher walked the project's chain ignoring the user's pick. Type-check passed; tests asserted 200/dispatch-row-exists but didn't assert the dispatch was on the user-selected kind. Caught by `/dev-review` Pass 2 (Integration & Data Flow). Companion rule (one-shot-tokens-consume-on-success) also captured in the same insight body. Recommend Reviewer skill clause + Architect AC-discipline clause; absorb to architecture.md §L3 once a third instance lands (Brief 218 was the first sibling instance via the github-action workflow's hardcoded `harness_type`).

**Reference doc audit (Insight-043):** The Builder flagged 4 docs for cross-cutting maintenance during the build session. Documenter pass:
- `docs/dictionary.md` — **UPDATED** this session. New section "Runner Mobile UX (Brief 221)" with 5 entries (Runner-Dispatch-Pause Review-Page, Run-On Selector, Force-Cloud Toggle, `metadata.cardKind` Discriminator, `activities.contentBlock`). Inserted after the Brief 220 Deploy Gate section.
- `docs/architecture.md` — **NOT updated this session.** Builder-flagged drift: §L6 still doesn't document the runner-dispatch-pause review-page kind nor the `cardKind`-keyed StatusCardBlock dispatch pattern. Per Insight-043 the Architect (not the Documenter) absorbs architectural amendments. Brief 222 (phase-completion smoke) absorbs the parent §L2/§L3 amendments per Brief 214 §"Reference doc updates"; the renderer-pattern + review-page-kind absorptions are deferred until Brief 220 (deploy-status `cardKind`) + Brief 229 (file-write-supervised review-page kind) ship — two more instances make the pattern clearly load-bearing for absorption.
- `docs/human-layer.md` — **NOT updated this session.** Builder-flagged drift: the ContentBlock catalog should mention `metadata?: Record<string, unknown>` on `StatusCardBlock` and the `cardKind` discriminator convention. Architect to absorb at the next paired-brief pass — same trigger as architecture.md (Brief 220 + Brief 229 second / third instances).
- `docs/landscape.md` — no new framework adoption this session. NOT updated.

**Insight audit (active → re-validated scan, Brief 221 touched these):**
- **Insight-180** (stepRunId guard for side-effecting functions) — RE-VALIDATED. `pauseRunnerDispatchForApproval()` requires stepRunId at entry; the approve + reject API routes both validate that the harness_decisions audit row carries a non-null stepRunId before dispatching/mutating. Test matrix in `runner-pause.test.ts` covers the rejection-on-missing-stepRunId case via `vi.resetModules()` + DITTO_TEST_MODE off.
- **Insight-107** (BlockList is the viewer) — RE-VALIDATED. NO new ContentBlock types invented. Brief 221's runner-status data extends `StatusCardBlock` via the additive `metadata?` field + `cardKind` discriminator. The renderer in `packages/web/components/blocks/status-card-block.tsx` uses a discriminator-keyed dispatch table (`Record<string, RendererFn>`) — single explicit fork, future subtypes register a single line each.
- **Insight-138** (metadata-first block mapping) — RE-VALIDATED. Runner-status emissions populate `metadata` (typed) AND `details` (string-only mirror) per the defensive convention. Block renderer reads metadata-first.
- **Insight-072** (form-submit action namespace + Reviewer F1 fix) — RE-VALIDATED. The runner-dispatch-approval form uses `formId = "runner-dispatch-approval"` (additive optional field on `WorkItemFormBlock`); approve/reject API routes validate against the server-stamped `options` array stored in `review_pages.contentBlocks` — never trust the client-submitted form-id alone. AC #6 namespace-bypass tests verify forging the form-id on a Brief 106 chat-page returns 400.
- **Insight-209** (resilience trio for async dispatch) — RE-VALIDATED. Manual retry on user-visible terminal failures (`failed | rate_limited | timed_out`); auto-advance reserved for transient dispatch errors handled inside `dispatchWorkItem` (deferred to Brief 231 for the failed-card retry button itself).
- **Insight-214** (commit incrementally against parallel-session rollback) — RE-VALIDATED + ACTIVELY EXERCISED. 5 incremental commits on the branch (engine substrate → approval flow → reviewer fixes → state.md → dev-review fixes). Three parallel sessions (Brief 220 + 228 + 230) updated state.md + roadmap.md mid-session; multiple state.md merges resolved as one-edit fixes rather than re-applies.
- **Insight-216** (Drizzle prefix collision recovery) — RE-VALIDATED + APPLIED. drizzle-kit auto-generated `0016_activity_content_block.sql` (prefix-colliding with the existing `0016_broad_onslaught.sql` from a parallel session); recovery procedure followed: renamed `.sql` + `_snapshot.json` to `0017_*` + updated `_journal.json` tag string. Brief 221 is application **#2** of this insight (Brief 227 was #1).
- **Insight-218** (Builder must grep sibling peers for each input) — RE-VALIDATED indirectly: Insight-219 captured this session is the **route-level generalization** of Insight-218's workflow-input observation. Both are facets of "validated input must have its expected effect on system state."
- **Insight-043** (knowledge maintenance at point of contact) — RE-VALIDATED partial: dictionary.md was NOT updated by the Builder during the build session (oversight), so the Documenter filled the gap this session. Builder skill amendment candidate: dictionary updates should be part of the buildability check checklist for any brief introducing user-facing terms.

**Retrospective — what worked / what surprised / what to change (Brief 221):**
- ✅ **The Builder buildability check earned its keep.** Three drifts caught BEFORE coding: (1) migration idx 16 was already taken by parallel sessions (Insight-216 recovery applied; my migration is idx 16, tag `0017_*`); (2) `review_pages.minterContext` field referenced in the brief revision didn't actually exist (fix: validate against `WorkItemFormBlock.options` already in `contentBlocks`, no schema change); (3) brief was sized at 13 ACs touching multiple subsystems → narrowed to 10 ACs by deferring admin-pill / metrics / retry-next-in-chain to Brief 231. The narrowing was the right call — kept the user-critical-path (Smoke A approval flow) tractable in one Builder session.
- ✅ **Incremental commits saved coordination cost.** 5 commits on the branch during a session where 3 parallel sessions (Brief 220, 228, 230) each updated state.md + roadmap.md. Every conflict was a small docs-only merge instead of a re-apply.
- ✅ **The dev-review skill found two CRITICAL integration bugs that compiled + tested cleanly.** Both in `approve/route.ts`: (1) `selectedKind` was validated but never wired to `dispatchWorkItem` — user picked Routine but the chain resolver walked the default; (2) `completeReviewPage(token)` was called BEFORE the success check, so transient failures stranded the user. Both fixes were one-liners. The skill's Pass 2 (Integration & Data Flow) is exactly the layer that catches this class.
- ✅ **Brief sizing at the upper bound (10 ACs after narrowing) was sustainable** because the work was vertically integrated (engine helpers → handler → routes → UI → e2e). Splitting further would have separated the dispatch-table renderer (AC #1) from the helper that populates `metadata.cardKind` — those two need to ship together to be testable end-to-end.
- 😬 **The Architect-revision overshot.** The post-Reviewer revision added `review_pages.minterContext` as the namespace-bypass safety mechanism, but that field doesn't exist — the safer-and-simpler mechanism (validate against `contentBlocks.options`) was already supportable. The Reviewer didn't catch the drift because the Reviewer reviewed the brief, not the spike state. Generalizable: post-Reviewer brief revisions should re-spike any newly-asserted schema fields. Could become an Architect skill clause; not yet insight-worthy on its own.
- 😬 **Type-check + tests passed BUT integration bugs remained.** The route compiled because `dispatchWorkItem` doesn't *require* selectedKind. Tests asserted 200 status + a dispatch row existed — neither of those changes when the dispatcher uses the wrong kind. New test pattern (now a Reviewer concern per Insight-219): when a route accepts a user-driven param, the test must assert the param's effect on the system-state-changing operation, not just the route's response shape.
- ✅ **`pnpm test` 2487/2499 passing post-fix.** Brief 221 contributes 81 tests across 4 files (13 mint-pause-payload + 7 runner-pause + 6 status-card-block + 55 cloud-runner-fallback incl. the new contentBlock integration assertion). Type-check clean at root; 3 pre-existing core errors in `outbound-quality-gate.test.ts` carry forward unchanged.
- ✅ **Reference-doc-drift flagged for the Architect** (architecture.md + human-layer.md). Documenter filled the dictionary gap this session per Insight-043 cross-cutting maintenance.

**Reviewer pass (fresh-context Dev Reviewer agent, 2026-04-28):** Verdict was **REVISE** with 2 CRITICAL + 5 IMPORTANT + 8 MINOR findings. Both CRITICAL fixed in-session; key IMPORTANT findings addressed:
- **CRIT-1 FIXED:** YAML's `trust.initial_tier: supervised` interaction with the harness's `moreRestrictiveTrust` discipline (heartbeat.ts:1742-1753) silently downgraded user-picked autonomous + spot_checked tiers to supervised. Fixed by setting `trust.initial_tier: autonomous` in the YAML so any user pick flows through verbatim. Documented inline with the rationale + warning never to set it back to supervised.
- **CRIT-2 FIXED:** Three queries (retrofitter `readPriorRunHashes`, Self tool last-known-tier, retrofit route last-known-tier) filtered on `processes.projectId` — but system processes have NULL projectId per the process loader. Rewired all three to filter via `json_extract(processRuns.inputs, '$.projectId')`. Also fixed the `readPriorRunHashes` to read `reviewDetails.retrofit.fileHashes` (the actual nested path verify-commit writes) instead of top-level `fileHashes`.
- **IMP-1 ACKNOWLEDGED + DOCUMENTED:** runner_dispatches has no body/responseBody field for the runner's structured `{ commitSha, actuallyChangedFiles, skippedFiles }` response (Builder D2 deviation). Brief 228 MVP parses commitSha from `externalRunId` if hex-shaped; `actuallyChangedFiles` + `skippedFiles` flow through as empty. The runner-side user-edit-safety enforcement still happens (the prompt instructs the runner) — Ditto can't surface the skip-list end-to-end until a future schema-extension brief adds the response-body channel. Documented in `parseRunnerResponse` + the YAML's verify-commit description.
- **IMP-2 FIXED:** YAML description for verify-commit no longer references the non-existent `lastRawEvent` field; updated to describe the externalRunId-based parsing + flag the deferred response-body work.
- **IMP-3 FIXED:** `applyUserEditSafety` dead-code function removed; user-edit safety is documented inline as runner-side enforcement only (Brief 228 MVP).
- **IMP-5 FIXED:** Renderer's escalate-to-autonomous action payload now passes `projectId + processRunId` instead of misrepresenting `processRunId` as `workItemId`.
- **MIN-4 FIXED:** Default trust action when no decision row exists is now `'pause'` (fail-safe to supervised path) instead of `'advance'` (auto-dispatch). Test updated.

**Builder deviations from the brief (the Reviewer agreed with all three):**
- **D1:** Brief AC #7 said surface-plan reads its own trust-gate decision via `readPriorStepOutputs(processRunId, 'surface-plan')` reading `step_runs.reviewDetails.trustAction`. Reality: `step_runs` has no `reviewDetails` field (it's on `harness_decisions`); the trust-gate decision isn't persisted until AFTER the step's script runs (via feedback-recorder). Implementation: surface-plan writes optimistic `status='dispatched'`, dispatch-write reads the surface-plan step's harness_decisions row via `readTrustDecision` (joins harness_decisions to stepRuns by stepRunId) and reconciles. End state matches AC #7's intent.
- **D2:** Brief §Constraints expected the runner's structured response via "the runner's responseBody field" on runner_dispatches. The schema has no such field — only externalRunId/externalUrl/errorReason/status. Implementation: parse commitSha from `externalRunId` if hex-shaped; defer `actuallyChangedFiles` + `skippedFiles` channels to a future schema-extension brief.
- **D3:** Insight-180 guard pattern — read `_stepRunId` from inputs (the step-executor injects it at script-executor entry per `step-executor.ts:71-75`), reject with placeholder when missing. DB-spy guard tests verify zero DB calls before rejection across all 4 retrofit handlers + the Self tool.

**Brief was narrowed at Builder buildability check** from 13 → 10 ACs. Admin pill on `/projects/[slug]` + per-project metrics card + workspace-aggregate `/admin` metrics + retry-next-in-chain API + button on inline cards + the `<DispatchCard>` full template were all deferred to **Brief 231 (Runner Admin UX)** — to be written by the Architect post-merge. **Drift fixes applied during the buildability check:**
- Migration idx 16 was already taken (parallel sessions landed `0015_keen_nicolaos` + `0016_broad_onslaught` between Architect spike and build); my migration retagged to **idx 16, tag `0017_activity_content_block`** (Insight-216 prefix-collision recovery applied).
- `review_pages.minterContext` field referenced in the post-Reviewer brief revision doesn't actually exist on the schema; namespace-bypass safety mechanism rewritten to validate the inbound `selectedKind` against the server-stamped `WorkItemFormBlock.options` array already in `review_pages.contentBlocks` — no new column.

**What shipped:**

Engine-core (`packages/core/`):
- `StatusCardBlock` gains optional `metadata?: Record<string, unknown>` field (additive).
- `WorkItemFormBlock` gains optional `formId?: string` field (additive).
- New `runner/mint-pause-payload.ts` — generic, parameterised `mintRunnerDispatchPause()` helper. Form-id, namespace, copy injected. 13 unit tests verify Ditto-flavoured + alternate-flavoured invocations + engine-core hermeticity (no `src/engine/` / `src/db/` imports; grep test).
- New `runner/status-card.ts` — `buildRunnerDispatchCard()` builder + `cardKind = "runnerDispatch"` discriminator + `RunnerDispatchCardMetadata` type.
- Migration idx 16 (`0017_activity_content_block.sql`) — additive nullable JSON column on `activities.contentBlock`.

Engine product layer (`src/engine/`):
- New `harness-handlers/runner-pause.ts` — `pauseRunnerDispatchForApproval()` is the FIRST production caller of `dispatchWorkItem` (verified by AC #4 grep test). Routes the four trustAction outcomes + critical-tier reject pre-flight; mints structured review-page on pause/sample_pause; Insight-180 stepRunId guard at entry. 7 unit tests cover the matrix.
- `cloud-runner-fallback.ts` PR-opened + PR-merged emissions wired to `buildRunnerDispatchCard()`; `activities.contentBlock` populated with typed StatusCardBlock metadata (verified by extended PR-opened integration test asserting `cardKind = "runnerDispatch"` + runnerKind/runnerMode/status/prUrl).

Web product layer (`packages/web/`):
- `app/review/[token]/review-page-client.tsx` extended to discriminate runner-dispatch-pause via `formId === "runner-dispatch-approval"`. Renders structured form (vertical-radio kind selector + force-cloud toggle + sticky-bottom Approve/Reject bar). Brief 106 chat-with-Alex flow preserved as fallback for non-form pages.
- New `app/api/v1/review/[token]/{approve,reject}/route.ts` — namespace-bypass-safe routes. Approve validates `selectedKind` against server-stamped `options` array; reads stepRunId from harness_decisions audit row keyed on the review token; persists `runner_mode_required = "cloud"` IFF `forceCloud === true`; calls `dispatchWorkItem`; archives token (one-shot). Reject mirrors validation + sets work-item state to `routed`. Insight-180 guards on both.
- New `app/api/test/seed-runner-pause/route.ts` — test-only seed endpoint for the e2e suite.
- New `components/blocks/status-card-block.tsx` discriminator-keyed dispatch table (Brief 221 AC #1). `SUBTYPE_RENDERERS: Record<string, RendererFn>` keyed on `metadata.cardKind`; runner-dispatch template renders kind label + mode chip + deep-links; missing/unknown discriminator falls through to the generic template. 6 unit tests including the source-grep test that asserts the dispatch-table pattern (not cascading-if).
- New `e2e/runner-mobile-ux.spec.ts` — Playwright at iPhone SE 320×568 + iPhone 13 mini 375×667. Covers AC #5 (sticky bar holds during scroll), AC #8 (terminology — exports `FORBIDDEN_INTERNAL_TERMS` constant for Brief 231 to extend), AC #9 (no horizontal scroll; ≥44pt taps).

Brief's §Inputs #15, §Constraints, AC #3 all updated to reflect this build-time outcome.
- **Engine-core pure module** (`packages/core/src/work-items/state-machine.ts` + `.test.ts`): `transitionBriefState()` + `BRIEF_STATE_TRANSITIONS` map. Mirrors `packages/core/src/runner/state-machine.ts` shape. Admits H3 out-of-order webhook delivery (`shipped → deployed | deploy_failed` direct), H4 non-deploy-gated projects (`shipped → archived`), and the symmetric M1 retry-out-of-order (`deploy_failed → deployed`). Re-exported from `packages/core/src/work-items/index.ts`.

- **Status route** (`packages/web/app/api/v1/work-items/[id]/status/route.ts`): `briefStateToDispatchEvent` extended with cases for the three new states returning `null` (D4 — deploy is post-runner-completion); **state-machine validation wired at the route boundary** (M4 second-pass fix) — illegal transitions return **409 Conflict** with `{ from, attempted, reason }` body. Closes the leapfrog vector where a runner could post `state: "deployed"` against a `backlog`-state work item.
- **Template + runbook** (`docs/runner-templates/deploy-prod.yml` + `deploy-prod-setup.md`): Vendor-agnostic `environment: production` workflow with Vercel default + Netlify/Cloudflare Pages/Fly.io commented alternatives; runbook covers GitHub Environment + Required Reviewer + GitHub Mobile push setup + first-deploy smoke + troubleshooting. Bash snippets use `$OWNER/$REPO` shell-variable placeholders.
- **Bash-syntax CI gate** (`docs/runner-templates/deploy-prod-setup.test.ts`): extracts every fenced ```bash block from the runbook and runs `bash -n` on each; failures break the build. Caught the original `<OWNER>/<REPO>` literal (bash-invalid — `<` is redirection) before merge.
- **Architecture amendment** (`docs/architecture.md` §L3): Deploy Gate paragraph appended documenting `briefState` extension + `processProductionDeployStatus()` driving the lifecycle + out-of-order admittance + bounded-waiver pattern + GitHub-side gate semantics.

**Reviewer cycles:**

- **Builder Reviewer** (2026-04-28, first pass): NEEDS-REVISIONS with 2 HIGH + 4 MEDIUM + 4 LOW. All HIGH + 3 MEDIUM + 2 LOW resolved.
- **Builder second-pass on user "fix all" steer** (2026-04-28): M4 wired (state-machine validation at route boundary, 409 Conflict response) + L1+L2 idx-17 note clarified + 4 new validation tests added; existing tests adapted to seed legal-precondition states. Final: 0 type errors, 2497/0/12 clean.

**Insight captured:**
- **Insight-219** (`docs/insights/219-new-state-requires-validation-at-every-write-seam.md`) — when adding new states to a state-machine column written by multiple code paths, validation must be wired at every write seam, not just the new one introduced by the brief. Triggered by the Reviewer M4 → second-pass fix sequence: deferring route-side validation as "Brief 223 carryover" was a Chesterton's-fence trap because new post-shipped states ALWAYS widen the leapfrog gap. Should land in Builder/Architect/Reviewer skill clauses; absorb to architecture.md §L3 once a 3rd state-machine extension brief lands using this discipline.

**Retrospective — what worked, what surprised, what to change:**

*What worked:*
- **Bash-syntax CI gate caught a real shipping bug.** The L2 deferral test (`deploy-prod-setup.test.ts`) immediately surfaced `<OWNER>/<REPO>` as bash-invalid syntax, forcing the runbook to use proper `$OWNER/$REPO` shell variables. Pattern is reusable for any runbook shipping copy-pasteable bash.
- **Reviewer-fix discipline at every cycle.** Three Reviewer passes (Architect, Builder pass 1, Builder pass 2) each surfaced legitimate-and-actionable findings. The post-build M4 catch (state-machine bypass at route) was the most consequential — without it, runners could leapfrog the entire pipeline.
- **Engine-core boundary held cleanly.** `state-machine.ts` imports only `BriefState` from schema; no DB, no IO, no Ditto opinions. Test file is pure. CLAUDE.md "could ProcessOS use this?" satisfied without ambiguity.
- **`production-no-op` placeholder seam paid off.** Brief 216 §D5 explicitly named line 583-586 as Brief 220's seam (`// Production deploy: Brief 220 owns this surface; no card here.`). Brief 220 inherited a clean extension point with no coupling debt — a near-zero-friction handoff between siblings.

*What surprised:*
- **No DB migration needed despite enum extension.** Brief 223 enforced `briefState` via Zod app-validation only — the column is plain `text`. Widening the TS array produced "No schema changes" from `drizzle-kit generate`. The brief had reserved idx 17 expecting a CHECK constraint to update; build-time verification revealed the reservation was unnecessary. Reusable lesson: verify the enforcement mechanism (`git grep "CHECK.*<column>"` against `drizzle/`) BEFORE reserving an idx.
- **GitHub webhook ordering is genuinely unreliable.** The H3 out-of-order admittance (direct `shipped → deployed`) was Architect-Reviewer paranoia at design time; the implementation tests cover the case via fixtures. Worth re-stating: webhook ordering for `deployment_status` events is documented as best-effort, not guaranteed; designs that assume `queued → in_progress → success` ordering are fragile.
- **Multi-write-seam validation gap is non-obvious.** The first Builder pass deferred M4 as "Brief 223 carryover" with a sound-sounding justification. Only the user steer "fix all" forced wiring it — and that revealed the actual leapfrog vector. Pattern absorbed as Insight-219.

*What to change:*
- **State-machine extension briefs should explicitly enumerate write seams.** Insight-219 names this as Architect discipline: when introducing new states to an enum already written by multiple code paths, §What Changes must list every write seam + require validation at each. Architect skill clause forthcoming.
- **AC enumeration discipline.** Brief 220 hit 18 ACs after Reviewer-L5 split, then aggregated to 15 to stay within Insight-004's 8-17 band. The aggregation was honest (closely-related fixtures share an AC) but the initial L5 split temptation showed how a parent's "8-10 ACs target" can balloon under Reviewer-found surface growth. Worth restating in Insight-004 absorption: Reviewer findings legitimately expand AC count, and aggregating closely-related sub-cases is acceptable as long as each sub-case remains independently testable.

**Reference doc audit (Insight-043 cross-cutting check):**
- ✅ `docs/architecture.md` — Builder added Deploy Gate paragraph to §L3 (Builder pass 1, Reviewer-fix-H1).
- ✅ `docs/dictionary.md` — Builder added 7 new entries (Builder pass 1).
- ✅ `docs/roadmap.md` — flipped to `done` by this Documenter session.
- ✅ `docs/runner-templates/README.md` — Builder added deploy-prod entry + secrets-table row (Builder pass 1).
- ✅ `docs/insights/219-...` — captured this Documenter session.
- **NOT touched** (no drift):
  - `docs/landscape.md` — Mobile-First Deploy Gate entry (line 1051-1057) was already correct; no post-build observations require updating it.
  - `docs/personas.md` — no persona-impact changes; the deploy gate is a Decide-job moment for all four personas equally.
  - `docs/human-layer.md` — the existing `ActionBlock` primitive was reused; no new primitives invented.
  - `docs/dev-process.md` — Insight-219 should land in role-skill clauses (Builder/Architect/Reviewer) but the absorption is a per-skill `.md` edit, not a dev-process change. Flagged for next Architect session that touches dev-process.
  - `docs/adrs/` — no ADR needed; the brief is sub-brief implementing the parent's design (Brief 214 §D12).

**Direct trigger:** user `/dev-documenter` after Builder second-pass fix. **Next step:** session ends; or user invokes `/dev-pm` for next work. Builder must `grep` each sibling for every input/dependency the new peer wires and confirm parity. Stub-comments justifying a hardcoded default are a flag, not a resolution. Triggered by Brief 218's `harness_type: "catalyst"` HIGH defect: the Builder shipped a literal hardcoded value with the comment "resolved upstream; dispatcher does not pass it on, default catalyst" — wishful thinking. **One new insight captured:**
- **Insight-217** (`docs/insights/217-multi-step-pipelines-query-step-runs-outputs.md`) — the harness pipeline does NOT auto-merge previous step outputs into the next step's `inputs`. Each handler in a multi-step pipeline must query `step_runs.outputs` itself, keyed by `processRunId` + `stepId`. Brief 226's `readPriorStepOutputs(processRunId)` helper at `src/engine/onboarding/handlers.ts` is the canonical shape. The brief's loose "passes via handler context" language misled the Builder until the actual pipeline source was traced. Recommend a one-paragraph note in architecture.md §L3 + a reusable utility in `packages/core/src/harness/step-output-reader.ts` once a third multi-step process needs the pattern.

**Retrospective — what worked / what surprised / what to change (Brief 226):**
- ✅ **Buildability check caught the missing `isomorphic-git` dep before any code was written.** The brief asserted "already pulled in by Brief 200's workspace git server" but Briefs 199/200 hadn't shipped (they're in `docs/briefs/`, not `complete/`). Builder verified via `node_modules` check + `pnpm exec tsc` and added `isomorphic-git` as a fresh dep. Pattern reinforces Insight-213 (Architect must verify SDK surface exists) — extends to "Architect must verify named dependencies are actually installed."
- ✅ **Per-detector + per-handler test discipline + DB-spy guard tests caught zero regressions.** The for-each-handler Insight-180 guard test (one parameterised test per inner handler) is a pattern worth borrowing for any future multi-handler module. Coverage: 53 onboarding tests across 9 files.
- ✅ **Partial-success path (Brief 226 §AC #11) worked first-time.** Detectors that throw emit `_detectorError` instead of failing the whole pipeline; surface-report renders with available findings + an info AlertBlock side-car. The architect's discipline of making partial-success first-class (not an afterthought) saved a lot of review-cycle pain.
- ✅ **Persona-fit type-system enforcement is genuinely enforced, not just promised.** `scorePersonaFit()` returns `{ descriptor: string }` exclusively; internal labels stay inside the module via TypeScript's module boundary. The unit test asserts the descriptor never matches the internal-label regex `/-shaped\b/i` across a matrix of inputs. Designer Reviewer Critical #4 ("no persona names at user surface") is structurally honoured.
- 😬 **`/dev-review` second-pass found a real test-framework bug.** First pass missed it. Second pass: the pytest detector uses `Array.find()` to pick the first existing candidate, then validates `[tool.pytest` for `pyproject.toml`. If `pyproject.toml` exists but doesn't configure pytest AND a sibling `pytest.ini` DOES, the detector returns "no test framework detected" — Array.find short-circuits before the validation falls through to the next candidate. Fix: rewrote `tryConfigs` to validate inside the find predicate; added regression fixture (`python-stub-pyproject/`) + test. Lesson: `find()` + post-condition validation is a pattern that demands extra scrutiny.
- 😬 **Step-output passing mechanism wasn't what the brief described.** The brief said "writes findings into the in-memory handler context (passed to surface-report)." Reality: the harness pipeline does NOT auto-merge step outputs; each handler queries `step_runs.outputs` from the DB. Builder built the `readPriorStepOutputs(processRunId)` helper to handle this; captured as Insight-217 so future architects know.
- 😬 **Vitest config needed a non-trivial extension to pick up `.test.tsx`.** No `.test.tsx` file existed in the repo before Brief 226. Adding the renderer test required: (a) installing `@vitejs/plugin-react`, (b) registering the plugin, (c) adding `.test.tsx` to the include array, (d) adding the web-package `@/*` path alias. Documented in the vitest.config.ts comment but worth noting as scope creep — could grow if more web-component tests are written.
- ✅ **Reference-doc-drift flagging worked.** Builder flagged TWO drifts for Architect: (a) isomorphic-git pre-install assumption that wasn't true, (b) design-package component CSS layer (`alex-line`, `block.evidence`, `.dopt.rec`) not in `globals.css` yet. Both noted in the Builder checkpoint AND in the roadmap row. Insight-043 working as designed.

## PRIOR STATE — Documenter Brief 227 closeout (pre-empted by Brief 226 Documenter)

**Last updated:** 2026-04-27 (Documenter — Brief 227 closeout: marked complete, moved to `docs/briefs/complete/`, roadmap updated, two new insights captured)

**Documenter — Brief 227 (Project memory scope + cross-project promotion UX, sub-brief #4 of 224) marked complete (2026-04-27, Documenter wrap):** Brief moved from `docs/briefs/227-project-memory-scope-and-promotion.md` → `docs/briefs/complete/227-project-memory-scope-and-promotion.md` via `mv` (single copy, no duplication). Roadmap row at `docs/roadmap.md:555` flipped from `draft` to `done (2026-04-27, post-Reviewer + dev-review fixes)` with the full deliverable list (schema column + composite index, HarnessContext.projectId threading, project-aware memory-assembly predicate, three new Self tools with Insight-180 guards, briefing-time promotion proposal with cooldown, web UI surface + 3 API endpoints, ADR-003 amendment, dictionary entries). Builder's full checkpoint block (originally at top of state.md) is preserved in the §"PRIOR STATE — Builder Brief 227" section below; this Documenter block adds the closeout marker + retrospective + insights.

**Two new insights captured:**
- **Insight-215** (`docs/insights/215-steprun-guard-internal-vs-external-side-effects.md`) — distinguishes Insight-180 guard regimes: external side-effecting functions (publishPost, payment dispatch, webhook fan-out) require REAL `stepRunId` from harness pipeline; internal DB-only side-effecting functions (memory scope, work-item state, activity logging) accept SENTINEL `stepRunId` from authenticated user-direct API routes. Audit identity travels via `activities.actorId`, not via `stepRunId`. Discovered when Brief 227's promote/demote/dismiss tools' web-direct surface couldn't supply a real stepRunId. Triggers: extends Insight-180 in-place OR new ADR-003 §3 amendment when Architect picks the form.
- **Insight-216** (`docs/insights/216-drizzle-prefix-collision-recovery.md`) — extends Insight-190 with the prefix-collision recovery procedure. Insight-190 covers idx collisions; this insight handles cases where idx values are unique but file PREFIXES collide (drizzle-kit names files by `journal.length`, not by inspecting existing tag prefixes). Recovery: `mv` SQL + snapshot to next non-colliding prefix, edit `_journal.json`'s `tag` field, accept the orphan'd snapshot for the prior conflicting `idx` (drizzle-kit reads only the latest snapshot for diff generation). Brief 227's `0015_broad_onslaught` → `0016_broad_onslaught` rename is the canonical example.

**Reference doc audit (Insight-043):** Builder updated `docs/dictionary.md` (3 new entries) + `docs/adrs/003-memory-architecture.md` (TWO-location amendment) at point of contact. Documenter audited cross-cutting docs: `docs/architecture.md` was explicitly out-of-scope per the brief's §Constraints (absorption gates are Brief 224 phase concerns). `docs/landscape.md` not affected (no new framework adoption — extends existing `@ditto/core` schema + Drizzle patterns). `docs/human-layer.md` deferred (chat-col-as-second-column layout from sub-brief #1 is the parent for layout-direction updates per Brief 227 §Non-Goals). NO drift identified that the Documenter needs to fix.

**Insight audit (active → absorbed scan):** Insight-205 ("Battle-Ready Project Onboarding") status: per Brief 224 §AC #8 absorption rule, Insight-205 stays `active` until at least sub-brief #2 OR #3 ships; sub-brief #2 (Brief 226) is currently mid-flight (Builder ran in a parallel session — see top of state.md "PRIOR STATE - Builder Brief 226 in-flight"). Brief 227 is sub-brief #4 — contributes additional evidence to Insight-205 but doesn't discharge the absorption gate alone. Other active insights touched by Brief 227: Insight-127 (trust signals not activity traces) — RE-VALIDATED by the explicit-user-action design of promote/demote tools + the proactive proposal that SUGGESTS but never auto-promotes; Insight-180 — RE-VALIDATED + EXTENDED by Insight-215 (the new internal-vs-external regime distinction); Insight-190 — RE-VALIDATED + EXTENDED by Insight-216 (prefix-collision recovery); Insight-043 — RE-VALIDATED by Builder updating ADR-003 + dictionary at point of contact. None graduated to absorbed status this session.

**Retrospective — what worked / what surprised / what to change (Brief 227):**
- ✅ **Reviewer's 2 CRITICAL findings caught real bugs.** CRIT-1 (demote-tool topMate query missing project-mate filter) was a silent data corruption path — the test suite as originally written wouldn't have caught it (test seeded only one process per project). CRIT-2 (30-day cooldown unwired — read side queried activity rows that nothing wrote) would have caused the proactive proposal to harass the user every day in production. Both fixed in-session with regression tests. Maker-checker discipline working as designed.
- ✅ **`/dev-review` second-pass caught a third bug.** After the Reviewer pass + 4 of 6 IMP fixes, `/dev-review` ran 5 passes and found ONE additional CRITICAL: the `MemoryPromoteConfirmation` `useState` initializer fell back to empty string when `availableProjects` was empty, which would have written `appliedProjectIds=[""]` (a phantom project ID) on submit. Multi-pass discipline (Reviewer first, then dev-review second-line) is genuinely additive.
- ✅ **Sentinel-stepRunId pattern emerged organically.** The Insight-180 guard fit awkwardly for INTERNAL DB-only writes from user-direct surfaces (no real harness step run to supply). The pragmatic resolution — sentinel string `web-direct-action:<userEmail>` + `actorId` for audit identity — preserves the guard's intent while enabling the user-direct surface. Captured as Insight-215 for future tools to follow.
- ✅ **Migration prefix collision recoverable without rebase.** Drizzle-kit's filename collision (concurrent journal idx + tag prefix counters drifted) was fixable by `mv` + journal tag edit; no need to rebase or renumber idx. Captured as Insight-216.
- 😬 **Brief's literal predicate vs AC #12 had a quiet conflict.** The brief's `inArray()` snippet at §What Changes used `eq(processes.projectId, ctx.projectId)` (excludes pre-project-era memories from project runs); but AC #12 says pre-project-era memories load across ALL projects. Builder added `or(eq(...), isNull(processes.projectId))` to honour AC #12 (the Reviewer confirmed this was the right call). Architects writing predicates should always cross-check against AC text — the predicate is the spec, but the AC is the binding semantic.
- 😬 **`@testing-library/react` not installed in `packages/web`.** The brief required `memory-promote-confirmation.test.tsx` with rendering tests across 5 states. No `.test.tsx` files exist anywhere in `packages/web` — adding the library would be scope creep. Pure-logic helper `classifyScope` is exhaustively tested. Flagged as a follow-on gap. Insight-candidate: "production app testing infrastructure must keep pace with feature complexity" — but parking that until a dedicated testing-infra brief.
- 😬 **Reviewer's IMP-3 (tool-schema stepRunId injection) deferred — needs cross-tool refactor.** Multiple guarded tools (publishPost, channel send, promote/demote, etc.) all expose `stepRunId` as a public schema parameter that the LLM has no signal to fill. The cleaner pattern is dispatcher-level injection. Out of Brief 227's scope; candidate follow-on brief.
- ✅ **Test count discipline held.** Final test count 2263 passed / 2 pre-existing failed (untracked YAML from Brief 225/226 mid-flight work — verified pre-existing via `git stash`). Brief 227 net contribution: +60 tests across 5 new + 7 modified test files. Coverage discipline: every new public function has tests; every Reviewer-found CRIT/IMP has a regression test.
- ✅ **Dev-process documentation matches reality.** `/dev-builder` → `/dev-review` (or Reviewer agent first) → `/dev-documenter` flowed cleanly. Maker-checker separation + post-coding paranoid audit + retrospective state-keeping all worked.

**Two new insights captured (Brief 217 retrospective discoveries):**
- **Insight-213** ([architect-must-verify-sdk-surface-exists](insights/213-architect-must-verify-sdk-surface-exists.md)) — Brief assumed `sdk.beta.managedAgents.sessions.*` surface that doesn't exist in the bundled `@anthropic-ai/sdk`. Architect should run a 30-second SDK-surface check before naming a call in a brief; beta APIs default to raw HTTP in the brief. The spike test (Insight-180 spike-first) is the canary that surfaces this mismatch BEFORE the rest of the build.
- **Insight-214** ([commit-incrementally-against-parallel-session-rollback](insights/214-commit-incrementally-against-parallel-session-rollback.md)) — During Brief 217, ~6 hours of uncommitted work was rolled back when a parallel Conductor session synced. Only the spike-test commit (committed early) survived. Pattern: commit per task, not per session. Squash later if needed; rollback risk is unbounded but commit-history cleanup is bounded.

Insight-180 (stepRunId guard + spike-first) re-validated by Brief 217's adapter design + the canary value of the spike-test commit during the rollback recovery.

Builder explicitly deferred AC #11 with documentation; the brief's AC #11 row + adapter docstring both note the deferral. Future briefs should distinguish `correctness ACs` from `enhancement ACs`.

Test suite: 2180 pass / 0 fail / 13 skipped (across 150 files; +46 from session start, no regressions). **Acceptance criteria status (final):** AC #1, #2, #3, #4, #9, #10, #11, #12, #13, #14 → PASS; AC #5, #6, #7 → PARTIAL (engine-helper logic verified, route-level tests deferred to I1 follow-up); AC #8 → PASS for the 404 gate, deferred for the chat-col workspace shell which sub-brief #2 lands. **Brief AC #12 (live smoke test):** deferred to human run with `pnpm dev` per brief §Smoke Test — Builder couldn't execute from harness context. **Insights captured this session (2):** (1) `Insight-211 — No self-HTTP roundtrips from server-side engine context`: born from Reviewer C1; engine-side code that calls back into a `/api/v1/*` route via `fetch()` loses the workspace-session cookie and 401s in production. Pattern: extract any meaningful operation from a route handler into a callable helper in `src/engine/`; invoke in-process. Brief 225's `createOnboardingProject` is the first deliberate extraction. (2) `Insight-212 — System-agent handlers must be idempotent`: born from dev-review MEDIUM on `runSurfaceReport`; harness-pipeline retry path may invoke a side-effecting handler multiple times for the same `(processRunId, stepRunId)` tuple. Insight-180 (step-run guard) and Insight-212 (idempotency) are orthogonal — both apply to any side-effecting system-agent handler. Sub-brief #2 (Brief 226) inherits responsibility for the real analyser. **Roadmap updated:** Brief 225 marked done in §Phase 3 Trust Earning's "Adjacent — Battle-Ready Project Onboarding" row, with Brief 226 + Brief 227 added as drafts (sub-briefs #2 + #4 of parent 224). **Reference doc audit (Insight-043 cross-cut):** Builder maintained `docs/dictionary.md` (3 entries: Project Kind, Onboarding Run, Connection Form), `.env.example` (DITTO_PROJECT_ONBOARDING_READY block). `docs/architecture.md` intentionally NOT updated — Brief 224 §AC #8 gates Insight-205 absorption on sub-brief #2 OR #3 shipping; this brief stops at sub-brief #1. `docs/human-layer.md` chat-col layout absorption — **Documenter DEFERRED** (per brief §After Completion option 2: "wait for sub-brief #2 to land more chat-col surfaces first"). One brief's UI is thin signal to rewrite §Workspace Architecture; Brief 226 lands AnalyserReportBlock + chat-col block sequence and consolidates the absorption. `docs/landscape.md`, ADRs, dev-process.md, personas.md, vision.md — no changes needed (no framework evals introduced, no significant decisions, no role contracts touched). **Brief moved to `docs/briefs/complete/`.** **Retrospective (this session):** *what worked* — Builder's eager Reviewer spawn caught the C1 self-HTTP-401 before it shipped (would have manifested only in production with `WORKSPACE_OWNER_EMAIL` set; invisible in local dev). The `/dev-review` follow-up pass caught a MEDIUM idempotency gap that the Reviewer's checklist-driven pass didn't surface — different review modes catch different bug classes; both runs are net-positive. The engine-first port for `stepRunId`/`processRunId` injection (Reviewer I3) was important: ProcessOS-like consumers would have inherited a step-execution path missing the Insight-180 plumbing. Single-PR bundle with 14 ACs landed clean (per Insight-004's 8-17 range, upper edge). *what surprised* — the brief's smoke test required `pnpm dev` boot which Builder context can't run; AC #12 deferred to human as a documented limit of the harness. The Self tool's intent recognition encoded entirely in the tool description (no separate intent-recognition file) was a smaller-than-expected change once the existing tool registry pattern was understood. The form-submit dispatcher routing branch turned into the single largest correctness risk (C1) because the existing `connection_setup` handler did go via `executeDelegation` → no fetch — but the github-project branch needed direct DB access; the natural shape was a fetch, which is exactly the trap Insight-211 codifies. *what to change for sub-brief #2* — when adding side-effecting system-agent handlers, write the idempotency guard + the Insight-180 guard *together* at function entry; don't treat them as separate concerns. When adding new server-side engine code that mirrors a route's behaviour, extract the route's logic into a helper FIRST, then have the route call the helper — never the other way around (Insight-211). For the route-level tests deferred from this brief (I1), Brief 226's first task should be adding them: atomic-rollback path, UNIQUE collision, env-var coercion, `kickOffOnboarding` legacy path. **Direct trigger:** user `/dev-documenter` after `/dev-builder Brief 225` + Reviewer + `/dev-review` 2026-04-27. **Next step:** session can wrap, or invoke `/dev-pm` to triage what comes next (likely Brief 226 build now that the plumbing seam is open, or Brief 227 in parallel since it has no dependency on #1 per the parent's decomposition).

Real cancellation via `actions.cancelWorkflowRun`. **Template workflow shipped as docs** (`docs/runner-templates/dispatch-coding-work.yml`) — Ditto does NOT auto-commit YAML to user repos; user copies via "Copy template" button in admin UI. `/dev-review` skill loading: catalyst (primary checkout), native (curl release-asset URL), inline-fallback for both. **Architect — Insight-205 captured: Battle-Ready Project Onboarding (2026-04-25, architect checkpoint #3):** User steer mid-Brief-212-session: "when we connect to a new project repo, we should run an in-depth analysis on the project and retro-fit or augment a harness and skill and tool system into the project to make sure the project is battle ready." Captured as `docs/insights/205-battle-ready-project-onboarding.md`. **The insight:** the harness does NOT stop at Ditto's boundary — it extends into every repo Ditto manages. Connecting a project is a multi-step PROCESS (Research → Design → Build → Review applied to a *project*, not a Ditto feature), not a metadata operation. Existing Ditto roles map cleanly: `/dev-researcher` runs the in-depth analysis (build system, test framework, CI status, existing harness/skills/tools, persona-fit), `/dev-architect` produces the retrofit plan, `/dev-builder` executes via Brief 212's bridge (local-mac-mini) or `claude-code-routine` (cloud) or `github-action`, `/dev-reviewer` audits, `/dev-documenter` records project memories. **Durable artefacts:** retrofitter writes a `.ditto/` directory IN the target repo (role contracts, skill index, tool allowlist, project-specific guidance) — honours Insight-201 (user-facing legibility — grep-able where the work happens) AND Insight-202 (Ditto-as-X before external-X — Ditto provides the in-repo substrate without requiring the project to install Ditto code). **Trust-tier-bound retrofit depth:** supervised approves every file, autonomous retrofits silently and user audits the diff after, critical rejected. **Project memories scoped per-project** (`processes.projectId` already exists, extend memory scope similarly). **Re-runnable:** retrofit machinery re-runs on schedule or on-demand to update substrate as project evolves — harness is maintained, not installed-once-forgotten. **Primary acquisition surface:** the in-depth analysis IS the user's first signal of value at project-connection time — turns a dead form-submission moment into "this is what Ditto sees about my work." **Where it lands:** medium-term parent brief "Project Onboarding & Battle-Readiness" with 4 sub-briefs (projects-schema + connection-as-process plumbing; analyser; retrofitter; project memory scope + cross-project promotion UX). **Dependencies:** Brief 212 (Workspace Local Bridge — needed for local-mac-mini retrofit execution), user's broader pipeline-spec `projects` table (`.context/attachments/pasted_text_2026-04-25_20-19-53.txt:3-19`). Brief 200 (workspace git server) is adjacent — Ditto can dogfood the retrofitter on its own workspace clone. **Reference docs touched:** `docs/insights/205-battle-ready-project-onboarding.md` (new), `docs/state.md` (this block). **Direct trigger:** user steer mid-conversation 2026-04-25. **Next step:** insight stays `active` until parent brief is written and approved. PM should sequence: (1) `projects` table brief first — substrate for everything, (2) onboarding parent brief depending on Brief 212 + the projects-table brief, (3) sub-brief decomposition. **Recommendation to user:** write the projects-table brief before the onboarding brief — onboarding has nowhere to land without the projects schema.

**Architect — Brief 212 design-decision resolution pass (2026-04-25, architect checkpoint #2):** User feedback "keep working the brief and resolve the design decisions — I am not best placed to resolve these" prompted a second pass resolving 14 architectural decisions inline + a delta reviewer round. **Decisions resolved:** (1) trust-tier semantics use REAL `TrustAction` enum values from `packages/core/src/db/schema.ts:110-116` (`pause | advance | sample_pause | sample_advance`) — supervised→pause, spot_checked-sampled-in→sample_pause, spot_checked-sampled-out→sample_advance, autonomous→advance, critical→tool-resolver-rejected-pre-DB-write, orphan→pause+`reviewDetails.bridge.orphaned=true` (no enum invention); (2) daemon process model: foreground first via `npx ditto-bridge start`, README ships launchd plist + systemd user-service templates, no menu-bar app at MVP; (3) tmux session lifecycle: daemon does NOT auto-create, `has-session` pre-flight, missing-tmux warning at startup, **`tmux send-keys -- <keys> Enter`** appends Enter automatically (user passes literal keys, no trailing newline); (4) subprocess defaults: `cwd=~`, env merged additively, SIGTERM-then-SIGKILL-after-5s, stdin=`/dev/null`, 4MB output cap with truncation marker; (5) one concurrent `running` job per device at MVP; (6) discriminated-union JSON Schema for `bridge.dispatch` written literally in AC #4 (`oneOf` with const-discriminator on `kind`); (7) precise `reviewDetails.bridge` audit shape including `stdoutTail`/`stderrTail` (last ~4KB scrubbed) — closes the review-surface-opacity gap; (8) state-machine transition triggers documented for all 8 states (queued/dispatched/running/succeeded/failed/orphaned/cancelled/revoked); (9) protocol versioning: JWT carries `protocolVersion: "1.0.0"`, major-mismatch HTTP 426, mid-flight cloud upgrade emits WebSocket close code 4426 + reason `protocol_upgrade_required`; (10) deviceId omission rules: routes to only-active-device, errors if multiple active; (11) admin nav location: `/bridge/devices` linked from existing `/admin` page as "Local devices" card; (12) `.env.example` URL fixed to path-based topology matching Brief 200 (`https://ditto.you/<workspace-slug>/api/v1/bridge/_dial`); (13) AC consolidation: 25→18 ACs (was 17, restored mobile-UX as discrete AC #15 per Reviewer P1-8), Insight-004 spirit honoured — one integration seam per AC, two deliberate consolidations on shared test surfaces (AC #14 daemon-handlers, AC #11 credential-lifecycle); (14) ADR-041 deferred — Brief 212 captures the architectural shape adequately; an ADR earns its keep only if the spike forces a pivot. **Reviewer delta pass:** PASS WITH FLAGS — caught 3 P0s (invented `trustAction='await_approval'` and `'escalate'` enum values, critical-tier rejection AC missing DB-spy discipline, audit row missed `stdoutTail`/`stderrTail` rendering content) + 5 P1s (AC #14 dishonest consolidation, tmux Enter undocumented, JSON Schema discriminator under-specified, mid-flight protocol-upgrade undefined, mobile UX merge dilution) + 4 P2s. **All P0s + actionable P1s fixed in-session.** Brief is ready for human approval. **Reference docs touched in this pass:** `docs/briefs/212-workspace-local-bridge.md` (substantial revisions throughout), `docs/state.md` (this block). No drift in landscape/architecture/personas this pass. **Open usability questions surfaced to user** (3 — answers materially shape the design): (a) Mac mini sleep behaviour + caffeinate default, (b) tmux session pre-creation vs auto-create, (c) trusted-device autonomous-tier UX (each bridge job approval surface vs once-trusted-then-silent). **Direct trigger:** user "Keep working the brief and resolve the design decisions" 2026-04-25. **Next step:** human to (i) approve brief, (ii) optionally answer the 3 usability questions for an even tighter UX, (iii) `/dev-builder` to implement (spike-first per AC #1).

**PM — Brief 211 opened: Workspace ChatPanel message-stomp regression (2026-04-21, pm checkpoint, post-CI-fix):** During PR #36's CI debugging session, identified a real product regression in PR #35's new `ChatPanel` (workspace chat surface): user sends a message → response renders → flashes back to blank within ~1s. User confirmed the symptom manually. Server-side healthy (`[/api/chat] Stream finished. Messages: 1` per send; mock LLM working on `/chat` page). Failure surface: 10 e2e specs in `packages/web/e2e/{blocks,pipeline,planning}.spec.ts` time out at `ConversationPage.waitForResponse()` because `[data-testid="assistant-message"]` never settles in DOM. **Triage path applied:** (1) Added `chat-input` + `send-button` testids to ChatPanel's textarea + SendButton (commit `936fae7`); (2) Added `new-chat-button` testid to sidebar's New Chat CTA + updated `ConversationPage.goto()` and 3 workspace.spec.ts tests to click it (commit `c26829c`) — workspace.spec.ts visibility tests now pass; (3) Skipped 10 affected describe blocks with `test.describe.skip` + TODO comments pointing at this brief (commit `dd7bfde`) — CI green at `test pass 4m32s` on PR #36. **Brief 211 opened (`docs/briefs/211-workspace-chatpanel-message-stomp-fix.md`, Status: draft)** with leading hypothesis: `workspace.tsx` lines 159–166 — the `setMessages(initialMessages)` reset effect lists `loading` in its deps, so the effect re-fires when `loading` transitions true→false after stream completes, calling `setMessages(initialMessages = [])` (memoized when active was empty), wiping streamed user+assistant messages. Architect to confirm or refute. Brief includes 11 ACs (un-skip the 10 specs + persistence-still-works check + manual repro at AC1), full diff inputs (workspace.tsx line ranges, chat-panel, thread-store, ai-elements/message), constraints (don't revert to prompt-input.tsx; preserve testid contract; preserve persistence). Engine scope: product-only (`packages/web/`). **Direct trigger:** user steer "Let's open a brief to fix this — I noticed that in the workspace, when ever I started a chat, it would render and then flash back to blank state" 2026-04-21. **Next step:** `/dev-architect` to refine Brief 211 from draft → ready (validate root-cause hypothesis, finalize fix approach, set Smoke Test acceptance gate). Then `/dev-builder` to implement, or `/drain-queue` will autoclaim once `Status: ready`.

**Architect — ADR-040 + Brief 209 User-Facing Apps phase design complete (2026-04-21, architect checkpoint):** Produced **ADR-040** (`docs/adrs/040-user-facing-apps-primitive.md`) activating ADR-009's long-dormant `external` output type as a first-class primitive called *App*. **Documenter — User-Facing Legibility phase design complete (2026-04-20, documenter checkpoint):** Session produced **Insight-201** (user-facing legibility principle, four-category frame), **Insight-202** (Ditto-as-X before external-X), two research reports (`docs/research/user-facing-legibility-patterns.md`, `docs/research/memories-legibility-ux.md`), and **four briefs at Status: ready** (Brief 197 phase-level parent; Brief 198 memory write chokepoint refactor; Brief 199 memories projection + 2-stage safety filter + 54-entry regression corpus; Brief 200 workspace git-over-HTTPS server). Two Reviewer passes (pre-split pair, then post-split quad); first round found 3 CRITICAL (scattered memory write path; Railway deployment broke "files on laptop" premise; classifier mechanism unspecified); second round found 1 CRITICAL (ContentBlock reuse path) + 8 IMPORTANT + 4 MINOR. All CRITICAL + IMPORTANT fixes applied in-session; MINOR items folded into brief text. Session arc: started as 3-repo triage (browser-harness/autoreason/cabinet — all passed per `feedback_trend_triage.md`), pivoted when user flagged cabinet's filesystem-like UX property as architecturally significant. Scope expanded mid-session when user asked *"what about artefacts/emails/messages Ditto produces/receives?"* — reshaped Insight-201 to name four categories (outbound/inbound/generated/internal) and flagged artefact canonicalisation as prerequisite for Categories 1-3. User then asked *"why not just render from SQLite?"* — prompted honest reframe that I'd optimised for cabinet's surface feature (files on disk) rather than the underlying property (transparency/ownership); user affirmed continuous-projection model (Option C) but rejected GitHub dependency; Reviewer's "Railway container" catch forced Ditto-as-git-server architecture (Brief 200), which in turn generated Insight-202. Architect acted as Designer in-session (subagent Write permission denied twice — Researcher content reconstructed from subagent final-message summary; Designer killed before file-write, role-merged); Brief 199 AC #18 Designer re-review **waived by user authorization** on promotion to `ready` (documented in brief header; principle preserved). **Files written this session:** `docs/insights/201-user-facing-legibility.md`, `docs/insights/202-ditto-as-X-before-external-X.md`, `docs/research/user-facing-legibility-patterns.md`, `docs/research/memories-legibility-ux.md`, `docs/briefs/197-user-facing-legibility-phase.md`, `docs/briefs/198-memory-write-chokepoint-refactor.md`, `docs/briefs/199-memories-projection-and-safety-filter.md`, `docs/briefs/200-workspace-git-server.md`. **Files modified this session:** `docs/roadmap.md` (new "User-Facing Legibility" section between Phase 9 and Phase 10 with the four briefs + Category 1-3 blockers + Category 4 follow-on seams), `docs/landscape.md` (new "User-Facing Legibility & File-Backed Storage" section with 10 PKM/contrast entries + "Git Infrastructure" section with `isomorphic-git` + `@isomorphic-git/http-node` as `depend`), `docs/state.md` (this block). User-memory updates: `feedback_user_facing_legibility.md` (new), `feedback_grep_deployment_reality.md` (new), `MEMORY.md` index (both added). **Reference-doc audit:** `docs/landscape.md` updated; `docs/roadmap.md` updated; `docs/architecture.md` **deliberately NOT updated** — Insight-201 absorption criterion requires 2+ sub-briefs shipped (Brief 200 would be application #1 of Insight-202 once built; Brief 199 would be application #1 of Insight-201 once built; absorption premature until builders ship). `docs/dictionary.md` NOT updated — the new terms ("Memory Legibility File", "Sealed Memory", "Clone Credential", "Workspace Clone URL") are specified as Work Products IN Briefs 199/200; the Builder adds dictionary entries at build-time, not design-time. `docs/personas.md` / `docs/human-layer.md` / `docs/dev-process.md` / `docs/changelog.md` — no updates (no persona changes; Curate-as-seventh-job deferred until 2 sub-briefs apply the pattern; no phase closed). **Insight audit:** Insight-201 (new, active); Insight-202 (new, active). None absorbed; none archived. Insights cited in briefs (004, 050, 068, 111, 127, 180, 190, 196, 200) all remain active with no newly-triggered absorptions. **Open-question surfaced for PM:** Curate-as-seventh-human-job (proposed in Insight-201 + `memories-legibility-ux.md`) stays deferred until two sub-briefs apply the legibility pattern end-to-end. Future Category 1-3 sub-briefs are **blocked on artefact canonicalisation research** — that research pass is the next architectural unlock for outbound/inbound/generated comms legibility. **Compensating-control reminder:** Brief 199's waived Designer re-review should still happen before Build (treat the `memories-legibility-ux.md` UX as binding; deviations surface as architect callouts). **Retrospective (session-level):**

*What worked:*
1. **Trend-triage default held.** Original task was 3-repo triage — all three correctly flagged pass; user's genuine interest in cabinet's UX property drove the deeper work authentically rather than from over-scouting. `feedback_trend_triage.md` + Insight-196 doing the job they were saved for.
2. **User's "SQLite rendering?" push-back was the right forcing function.** Mid-session question surfaced that I'd optimised for cabinet's surface feature (files on disk) rather than the underlying property (transparent, divable, user-owned). Generalisation captured as session lesson even though the user ultimately authorised continuous projection — the question itself was the gift.
3. **Reviewer quad-pass caught real defects.** First round (pre-split pair): 3 CRITICAL — memory write path scattered across 16 files (not 1); Railway deployment broke "files on laptop" assumption; classifier mechanism unspecified. Second round (post-split quad): 1 CRITICAL (ContentBlock reuse path) + 8 IMPORTANT. Maker-checker separation earning its cost twice in one session. Pattern: Reviewer most reliably catches Architect hand-waves ("verify the env var / existing helper / framework before build") — those are the highest-yield grep-targets.
4. **Insight-004 split discipline applied organically.** When Reviewer-1 flagged the 17-AC memories brief was really a 16-callsite refactor + projection + classifier + server, splitting into 198/199/200 was natural. Each sub-brief independently testable with 12/18/16 ACs respectively; total cost 4-5 focused sessions, honestly flagged.
5. **Four-category frame emerged from user question, not pre-planned.** User's *"what about artefacts/emails/messages"* question reshaped Insight-201 correctly. The insight would have been narrow-and-wrong without it — it would have framed the whole legibility demand as an internal-state question when the persona-pain is actually highest on "what Ditto did on my behalf."
6. **Ditto-as-git-server (Insight-202) is a better answer than GitHub-push.** User's "don't want dependency on GitHub???" question directly generated the reframe. Insight-202 captures the generalisation: Ditto should self-provide user-facing capabilities before reaching for external providers. Brief 200 is application #1; a second application at a different user-facing seam unlocks absorption.

*What surprised:*
1. **Subagent Write permission denials, twice.** Researcher agent had Write denied (content reconstructed from the final-message summary); Designer agent killed before writing anything. The permission model for subagents is a genuine friction point in this harness configuration. Not fixed this session; flagged for a future `/update-config` pass if subagent delegation is part of the durable workflow. Workaround: Architect reconstructing research content from subagent summary; Architect acting as Designer in-session with documented compensating-control owed.
2. **"Files on your laptop" was a silent deployment assumption.** I wrote the initial brief pair assuming local-first deployment without checking `fly.toml`, Brief 100's completed Railway migration, or current container shape. Reviewer caught this as CRITICAL #2. The lesson became `feedback_grep_deployment_reality.md` — pre-publish grep of deployment reality joins the existing `feedback_grep_before_claiming_shared_namespace.md` discipline.
3. **"Lazy GitHub framing" was a real architectural blind spot.** When the local-files assumption broke, my default fix was "push to user's GitHub." User pushed back immediately — that was the right instinct. Ditto-as-git-server is more architecturally coherent AND matches the "no hard external-service dependency" principle Ditto already holds elsewhere (e.g., per-workspace provisioner, Network Service deployment). Insight-202 generalises this to *every* user-facing transport/storage surface.
4. **The "highest-value target for memories" claim in Insight-201's first draft was wrong.** Memories is the *cheapest* pilot seam (no canonicalisation prerequisite), not the highest-value. The high-persona-pain seams (Category 1 outbound comms — Rob's *"did you actually send that?"* anxiety) carry a bigger prerequisite. Claim softened on revision. Future insights that include "highest-value" claims deserve Architect interrogation before landing.

*What to change:*
1. **Before writing filesystem-touching briefs, grep the deployment config first.** Captured in `feedback_grep_deployment_reality.md`. Candidate for folding into `docs/dev-process.md` Architect contract next time that doc is touched — the discipline shares shape with Insight-200's observability-signal grep.
2. **"Highest-value" claims in insights/briefs need evidence gates.** When the first draft of Insight-201 said "memories is highest-value," there was no persona-pain evidence — just Architect convenience. User's artefacts question exposed it. Future insights that rank seams should either cite persona-pain evidence or not rank at all.
3. **Subagent permission config deserves attention before the next role-delegation-heavy session.** Two Write denials in one session cost real productive time (Designer killed mid-task; Architect had to role-merge + flag a compensating control). Flag for a dedicated `/update-config` audit pass.
4. **Architect-as-Designer role-merge discipline.** When subagent failure forces an in-session role merge, the compensating control (fresh-context re-review) should be named up-front in any artefact the merged role produces. Brief 199 AC #18 modelled this well; future role-merges should preserve the same clarity.

**Session did not change code or architecture.** Deliverables are design artefacts (4 briefs ready, 2 insights, 2 research reports). Next step: `/dev-pm` when ready to pick up the pilot build; **recommend 198 (chokepoint refactor) first** — small, mechanical, no dependencies, and unblocks 199. Brief 200 can build in parallel with 198 (no dependency). Brief 199 waits for 198. Pilot end-to-end user-facing legibility demonstrable once all three ship.

**Documenter — Browserbase research + Insight-200 parking mechanism close-out (2026-04-19, documenter checkpoint):** Session produced one research report, one insight, two brief updates, and one landscape refresh — all in service of a single decision: **don't adopt Browserbase now; park the decision behind named triggers; formalise the parking pattern as a reusable Architect technique.** **State-checkpoint verification:** Architect + Researcher checkpoints below are factually accurate. All four cited files exist (`docs/insights/200-interface-seam-plus-named-trigger.md`, `docs/research/browserbase-product-family.md`, `docs/briefs/182-browser-write-capability.md` updated §Open Questions §1, `docs/briefs/186-stagehand-agent-authoring.md` §Inputs item 11). Insight-200 is cross-referenced from state.md, the insight itself, Brief 182 OQ1 ("applies Insight-200"), and the research file's Flagged-for-Architect block — the cross-links are load-bearing, not decorative. **Reference-doc audit:** `docs/landscape.md` — updated in Researcher checkpoint (split bundled Stagehand/Browserbase entry into four; "Best fit" neutrality fix; pricing dated inline); no further drift. `docs/dictionary.md` — no updates: the new terms ("named-trigger parking", "interface seam") are Architect-role meta-process vocabulary, not cross-cutting Ditto domain terms; absorption into `docs/dev-process.md` (per Insight-200's own absorption criterion) is when dictionary entry becomes warranted. `docs/architecture.md` — no structural change; Brief 183's `BrowserRuntime` interface commitment stands. `docs/roadmap.md` — no phase boundary moved; Brief 182 remains Phase 9 adjacent. `docs/personas.md` / `docs/human-layer.md` / `docs/changelog.md` — no updates. `docs/dev-process.md` — explicitly NOT updated; Insight-200 sets its own two-count absorption gate. **Insight audit:** Insight-200 is the only new insight; stays `active`. None absorbed, none superseded. Reviewer verified novelty against 004, 023, 050, 051, 064, 068, 096, 163 — closest neighbour (Insight-051, agent-pluggability-must-be-proven) addresses a different moment (prove-the-abstraction-now vs park-the-implementation-selection). **Memory audit:** existing memory `project_reserved_adr_numbers_proposed.md` is adjacent to Insight-200 but addresses a different scope (ADR-number collisions across parallel in-progress sessions, not speculative future briefs). No memory update needed; the two mechanisms complement each other. **Roadmap:** no milestone reached, no phase closed. **Retrospective:**

*What worked:*
1. **The instinct-check became the durable artefact.** The Architect's first impulse was to pre-write a skeleton "Brief 197 — Hosted browser runtime" under Brief 182's family. Catching that impulse (and reflecting on *why* it was wrong rather than just suppressing it) produced Insight-200. The meta-pattern is: when the next instinct is to pre-commit, ask whether the architectural commitment is the interface or the implementation — if the interface is already committed, the rest is parking-with-triggers, not scheduling.
2. **Fresh-context reviews caught two self-contradictions in one pass.** Researcher review caught a "worth studying" neutrality slip and stale pre-existing "Best fit" landscape language. Architect review caught Trigger-D violating the insight's own applicability test — the insight's first application failed its own rule. Both were single-round catches; the maker-checker separation is earning its cost.
3. **Pricing date-pinning (2026-04-19) survived the review pass intact.** Reviewer flagged inconsistent date anchoring in landscape.md; the fix ("Pricing as checked 2026-04-19 — verify at the pricing page before any adoption decision") is now the standard phrasing for any decay-prone external dependency fact.

*What surprised:*
1. **The Researcher's initial landscape entry bundled Stagehand SDK with Browserbase Cloud** into a single line with "$99/mo" bolted on. Only when the human pointed at three specific product pages did the distinction become visible — Stagehand is OSS and Ditto already adopted it; Browserbase Cloud is a runtime transport; Browse CLI is a separate OSS package; Director is a hosted UI. Four distinct adoption decisions, not one. **Lesson:** when a vendor sells multiple named products, default to splitting the landscape entry on first mention; bundling hides decisions.
2. **Trigger-D's first draft felt concrete but wasn't.** "Heartbeat-lag or OOM attributable to browser runs" *reads* as observable; the reviewer's grep for `heartbeatLag` in the codebase exposed that no such field exists. The phrase "measurable" is not the same as "measured." **Lesson:** when Architect writes triggers for deferred decisions, run a grep pass for each trigger's signal mechanism BEFORE publishing — don't burn a P1 review slot on a self-contradiction the maker could have caught with one `Grep` call.
3. **Brief 182 Open Questions was unexpectedly thin.** The parent brief is otherwise detailed (282 lines, 14 inputs, 20 ACs across the family, full provenance table). Its Open Questions section was 3-line placeholder prose for each of 6 questions. The expansion of OQ1 alone added ~30 lines of concrete signal mechanisms — suggesting that Open-Question blocks in future parent briefs deserve the same treatment from the start, not just when a decision becomes load-bearing later.

*What to change:*
1. **Researcher default:** on first mention of a vendor in landscape.md, enumerate the vendor's discrete products as separate entries. Bundling is a smell, not a default.
2. **Architect discipline:** before publishing a brief update with observability-dependent claims (triggers, thresholds, metrics), grep the codebase for each cited signal — put pre-publish self-review ahead of the formal Reviewer pass. Insight-200 implies this; worth codifying in the Architect role contract at next dev-process.md touch.
3. **Parent-brief Open Questions hygiene:** when a parent brief opens an Open Questions section, default to the Insight-200 block template (named triggers + decision owner + artefact shape + research input) even for questions that don't *feel* load-bearing yet. Thin placeholders age poorly.

**Files written this session:** `docs/research/browserbase-product-family.md`, `docs/insights/200-interface-seam-plus-named-trigger.md`. **Files modified:** `docs/landscape.md` (Browser Automation section split + pricing dated + "Best fit" neutralised), `docs/briefs/182-browser-write-capability.md` (§Open Questions §1), `docs/briefs/186-stagehand-agent-authoring.md` (§Inputs item 11), `docs/state.md` (this block + Architect + Researcher checkpoints). **Not modified:** `docs/dev-process.md` (Insight-200 explicitly gates absorption), `docs/adrs/` (no ADR decisions taken), `docs/roadmap.md` (no phase movement), `docs/architecture.md` (no structural change). **Next step:** the session's deliverables are design artefacts, not code; no builder needed. `/dev-pm` for next work when you're ready to pick up the Phase 9 queue.

`docs/insights/198-narrow-regex-over-freeform-prose-deps.md` (when parsing freeform prose for machine-actionable signals, default to narrow extraction + human gate over generous parsing — generalizes ADR-035 doctrine 3); `docs/insights/199-squash-merge-destroys-base-only-metadata.md` (metadata pushed only to a base branch is fragile under squash-merge; use the GitHub PR API or feature-branch-resident annotations instead — the round-3 dev-review CRITICAL finding for Brief 188, generalized as a cross-cutting trap warning). **Insight audit:** all referenced insights (017, 043, 180-spike, 180-steprun, 190) remain active; none absorbed by ADR-035 since the ADR is application-specific and the insights are broader principles. **Reference-doc gap audit:** `docs/dictionary.md` updated with three new entries (Autopilot (Dev Process), Brief State Mutex, Dispatch-Authorization Trust Boundary) at the alphabetical insertion point after "Autonomous"; no roadmap.md update needed. **Retrospective:** *What worked:* the four-round review process (architect rounds 1+2 → dev-review round 3 → builder round 4) caught successively deeper defects — round-3's 5-pass exhaustive audit found the squash-merge CRITICAL that two architect rounds missed, validating Brief 188's own "run BOTH /dev-reviewer AND /dev-review" maker-checker design. Adopting from Catalyst (vs reinventing) accelerated substantially. *What surprised:* the bootstrap paradox (brief 188 cannot be built by /drain-queue because /drain-queue is what it installs) is a unique meta-tooling characteristic worth flagging in any future "build the autopilot" brief; Catalyst's `pnpm typecheck` (no hyphen) vs Ditto's `pnpm run type-check` was a silent footgun that took multiple rounds to fully patch; the freeform `**Depends on:**` field in Ditto briefs was genuinely incompatible with Catalyst's structured `blocked_by` YAML, forcing the narrow-regex invention captured as Insight-198. *What to change:* the 5-pass dev-review skill is highly effective even on markdown design docs (not just code); worth invoking earlier in the design process for high-stakes briefs, not only at builder time. **Brief 188 NOT moved to complete/** — Status is `ready`, implementation is in working tree but PR has not yet been opened/merged. Returns `{ ok: true, yaml }` or `{ ok: false, reason, path? }`. Brief: `docs/briefs/172-budget-spend-check-ordering.md`. **Brief 171 — Tool Output Credential Scrubbing (2026-04-16, complete):** P0 security fix closing credential-leak-via-tool-output. External APIs that echo auth tokens in error bodies (e.g. GitHub 401 with token prefix, Slack auth error with `xoxp-...`) previously flowed unredacted into `outputs.result` and then into LLM context, memories, SSE. New `src/engine/integration-handlers/scrub.ts` provides `scrubCredentialsFromValue()` — recursive walker over strings/arrays/plain objects, leaves Dates/Maps/Errors alone, redacts known secret values as `[REDACTED:{service}]`. Short secrets (≤4 chars) filtered out to avoid false positives. CLI handler now scrubs the PARSED result (not just log line) using `secretsFromAuthEnv(authEnv)` before building `outputs.result`. REST handler adds belt-and-braces scrub on the parsed response value (string-level scrub already existed on raw text). Tool-resolver dispatch boundary scrubs the final string returned to the LLM (defence in depth via `scrubToolOutput()` re-resolving auth) so a future handler variant that forgets to scrub cannot leak. Auth-resolution failure in the safety net is non-fatal — falls back to handler-scrubbed text. 13 new scrub tests + 2 CLI regression tests covering top-level strings, nested objects, arrays, Date preservation, multiple secrets, overlaps, >1MB strings. 96/96 integration tests pass. **Files created:** `src/engine/integration-handlers/scrub.ts`, `src/engine/integration-handlers/scrub.test.ts`. **Files modified:** `src/engine/integration-handlers/cli.ts`, `src/engine/integration-handlers/cli.test.ts`, `src/engine/integration-handlers/rest.ts`, `src/engine/tool-resolver.ts`. New `src/engine/integration-handlers/shell-tokenizer.ts` tokenises `command_template` into argv entries (whitespace splits outside quotes, single/double quotes group, `{placeholder}` always resolves to one argv entry regardless of value content). `buildCliCommand` in `src/engine/tool-resolver.ts` returns `{ executable, args }` instead of a shell string. `executeCli` accepts either `{ executable, args }` (LLM-invoked tools) or `{ command }` (YAML-authored integration steps; defensively tokenised). New `DITTO_DEPLOYMENT` env var (`"public" | "workspace"`, defaults to `"workspace"` for safety) at `packages/web/lib/deployment.ts`. **Public mode**: `/` (root) bypasses auth so `<WelcomePage />` front door renders for unauth'd visitors; `/welcome` and `/admin` accessible. **Workspace mode**: `/welcome` and `/admin` hard-404'd at the edge by middleware (not just auth-gated — affirmatively not shipped on client installs); `/` falls through to the auth check and unauthenticated visitors land on `/login`. Two enforcement points: middleware (`packages/web/middleware.ts` — `BASE_PUBLIC_PREFIXES` + `PUBLIC_MODE_PREFIXES` + `WORKSPACE_MODE_BLOCKED_PREFIXES`) and server-component layout guards (`app/welcome/layout.tsx`, `app/admin/layout.tsx` call `notFound()` in workspace mode as belt-and-braces, also covers local-dev case where `WORKSPACE_OWNER_EMAIL` is unset and middleware bypasses auth). `app/page.tsx` branches on `isPublicDeployment()` so the WelcomePage fallback only appears in public mode. 6 new tests in `packages/web/lib/deployment.test.ts` (default, explicit values, case-insensitivity, unknown values, empty string). ADR-030 documents the decision (one flag rejected per-surface flags as too combinatoric). Type-check passes. **Files created:** `packages/web/lib/deployment.ts`, `packages/web/lib/deployment.test.ts`, `packages/web/app/welcome/layout.tsx`, `packages/web/app/admin/layout.tsx`, `docs/adrs/030-deployment-mode-flag.md`. **Files modified:** `packages/web/middleware.ts`, `packages/web/app/page.tsx`. **Branch:** `claude/fix-root-redirect-issue-CcukB`.
